There are many good introductory books on Buddhism which can be used to supplement the basic sketch provided in this volume. These 
include: 

Peter Harvey, [3mAn Introduction to Buddhism: Teachings, History and Practices [0m(Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 2012). 

[1m*Damien Keown and Charles Prebish, [3mIntroducing Buddhism [0m(London: Routledge, 2009). 

Donald W. Mitchell [3mIntroducing the Buddhist Experience [0m(Oxford: Oxford University Press, 2007). 

R. H. Robinson, W. L. Johnson, and Thanissaro Bhikkhu, [3mBuddhist Religions: A Historical Introduction [0m(Belmont, CA: Wadsworth 
Publishing Co. Inc., 2003). 

A lavishly illustrated introduction with chapters contributed by a range of specialists on the various Buddhist cultures is: 

Heinz Bechert and Richard Gombrich (eds.), [3mThe World of Buddhism: Buddhist Monks and Nuns in Society and Culture [0m(London: Thames 
and Hudson, 1984). 

A very good short introduction to the Buddhaโs life and social context may be found in: 

M. Carrithers, [3mThe Buddha: A Very Short Introduction [0m(Oxford: Oxford University Press, 2001). 

For an excellent introduction to Theravฤda Buddhism see: 

Richard Gombrich, [3mTheravada Buddhism: A Social History from Ancient Benares to Modern Colombo [0m(London: Routledge, 1988). 

For a more detailed account of the formative phase of Buddhism in India see: 

Rupert Gethin, [3mThe Foundations of Buddhism [0m(Oxford: Oxford Paperbacks, 1998). 

Paul Williams, Anthony Tribe, and Alex Wynne, [3mBuddhist Thought: A Complete Introduction to the Indian Tradition [0m(London: 
Routledge, 2011). 

For a more advanced account of Mahฤyฤna Buddhist thought see: 

Paul Williams, [3mMahayana Buddhism: The Doctrinal Foundations [0m(London: Routledge, 1989). 

For an illuminating guide to the spread of Buddhism: 

E. Zรผrcher, [3mBuddhism, its Origins and Spread in Words, Maps and Pictures [0m(New York: Routledge and Kegan Paul, 1962). 

The subject of Buddhist art and iconography is addressed in: 

D. L. Snellgrove (ed.), [3mThe Image of the Buddha [0m(London: Serindia Publications, 1978). 

Tibetan Buddhism is discussed in: 

John Powers, [3mConcise Introduction to Tibetan Buddhism [0m(Ithaca, NY: Snow Lion Publications, 2008). 

[1m*Geoffrey Samuel, [3mIntroducing Tibetan Buddhism [0m(London: Routledge, 2012). 

On Buddhism in China: 

K. K. S. Chโen, [3mBuddhism in China: A Historical Survey [0m(Princeton: Princeton University Press, 1964). 

E. Zรผrcher, [3mThe Buddhist Conquest of China [0m(Leiden: Brill, 1959). 

On Buddhism in its Chinese context see: 

[1m*Mario Poceski, [3mIntroducing Chinese Religions [0m(London: Routledge, 2009). 

Buddhism in Japan is treated in: 

J. M. Kitagawa, [3mReligion in Japanese History [0m(New York: Columbia University Press, 1966). 

On Buddhism in its Japanese context see: 

[1m*Robert Ellwood, [3mIntroducing Japanese Religion [0m(London: Routledge, 2007). 

On Buddhist meditation: 

Sarah Shaw, [3mIntroduction to Buddhist Meditation [0m(London: Routledge, 2008). 

A good, practical guide to Buddhist meditation is: 

Kathleen McDonald, [3mHow to Meditate [0m(London: Wisdom Publications, 1984). 

An ethnographic account of meditation practice in a Thai monastery can be found in: 

Joanna Cook, [3mMeditation in Modern Buddhism: Renunciation and Change in Thai Monastic Life [0m(Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 
2010). 

For information on the link between Buddhism and Neuroscience, consult: 

Allan B. Wallace, [3mContemplative Science: Where Buddhism and Neuroscience Converge [0m(New York: Columbia University Press, 2006). 

James H. Austin, [3mZen and the Brain: Toward an Understanding of Meditation and Consciousness [0m(Cambridge, MA: MIT Press, 1999). 

Kelly Bulkeley (ed.), [3mSoul, Psyche, Brain: New Directions in the Study of Religion and Brain-Mind Science [0m(Basingstoke: Palgrave 
Macmillan, 2005). 

On ethics: 

Damien Keown, [3mBuddhist Ethics: A Very Short Introduction [0m(Oxford: Oxford University Press, 2005). 

Peter Harvey, [3mAn Introduction to Buddhist Ethics: Foundations, Values and Issues [0m(Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 2000). 

H. Saddhatissa, [3mBuddhist Ethics: Essence of Buddhism [0m(London: Wisdom Publications, 1987). 

Roshi Philip Aitken, [3mThe Mind of Clover: Essays in Zen Buddhist Ethics [0m(Berkeley, CA: North Point Press, 1984). 

The subject of Buddhism and war is dealt with in the following: 

Brian Daizen Victoria, [3mZen at War [0m(Lanham, MD: Routledge, 2006). 

Michael K. Jerryson and Mark Juergensmeyer, [3mBuddhist Warfare [0m(New York: Oxford University Press USA, 2010). 

Xue Yu, [3mBuddhism, War, and Nationalism: Chinese Monks in the Struggle Against Japanese Aggression 1931โ1945 [0m(London: Routledge, 
2005). 

Tessa J. Bartholomeusz, [3mIn Defence of Dharma: Just-War Ideology in Buddhist Sri Lanka [0m(London: Routledge, 2002). 

A free online resource providing scholarly articles on Buddhist ethics is [3mThe Journal of Buddhist Ethics [0m
(http://blogs.dickinson.edu/buddhistethics). 

On the role of women in Buddhism: 

Rita M. Gross, [3mBuddhism After Patriarchy: A Feminist History, Analysis, and Reconstruction of Buddhism [0m(Albany, NY: State 
University of New York Press, 1993). 

Diana Y. Paul, [3mWomen in Buddhism: Images of the Feminine in the Mahayana Tradition [0m(Berkeley, CA: University of California Press, 
1985). 

Karma Lekshe Tsomo, [3mBuddhism Through American Womenโs Eyes [0m(Ithaca, NY: Snow Lion Publications, 2010). 

On the female founders of the Tantric Buddhist movement: 

Miranda Shaw, [3mPassionate Enlightenment: Women in Tantric Buddhism [0m(Princeton, NJ: Princeton University Press, 1995). 

On the movement for full restoration of ordination for nuns, see: 

Thea Mohr, Ven. Jampa Tsedroen, [3mDignity and Discipline: Reviving Full Ordination for Buddhist Nuns [0m(Somerville, MA: Wisdom 
Publications, 2010). 

The following discuss various aspects of the role of Buddhism in the modern world: 

H. Dumoulin (ed.), [3mBuddhism in the Modem World [0m(London: Collier Macmillan Limited, 1962). 

P. C. Almond, [3mThe British Discovery of Buddhism [0m(Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 1988). 

Robert Bluck, [3mBritish Buddhism: Teachings, Practice, and Development [0m(London: Routledge, 2006). 

Ken Jones and Kenneth Kraft, [3mThe New Social Face of Buddhism: A Call to Action [0m(Somerville, MA: Wisdom Publications, 2003). 

[1m*Charles S. Prebish, [3mAmerican Buddhism [0m(Belmont, CA: Duxbury, 1979). 

Charles S. Prebish and Kenneth K. Tanaka (eds.), [3mThe Faces of Buddhism in America [0m(Berkeley, CA: University of California Press, 
1998). 

Charles S. Prebish, [3mLuminous Passage: The Practice and Study of Buddhism in America [0m(Berkeley, CA: University of California Press, 
1999). 

Dharmachari Subhuti, [3mBuddhism for Today: A Portrait of a New Buddhist Movement [0m(Salisbury: HarperCollins Distribution Services, 
1983). 

The best way to learn about Buddhism is to read the Buddhaโs teachings. The standard complete translation of the Pali Canon, by 
various authors, is that published by the Pali Text Society but more recent translations are available from Wisdom Publications in 
the [3mTeachings of the Buddha [0mSeries. 

Anthologies of the early scriptures can be found in: 

Rupert Gethin (trans.), [3mSayings of the Buddha: New Translations from the Pali Nikayas [0m(Oxford: Oxford University Press, 2008). 

Bhikkhu Bodhi, [3mIn the Buddhaโs Words: An Anthology of Discourses from the Pali Canon [0m(Somerville, MA: Wisdom Publications, 2005).
